Industry and Commerce Department Shanghai Office Discusses Silver Prices 142

Over Ten Business Leaders from France, Japan, Germany, and Italy Arrive

Mitsui Bank President Tsuchiya Proposes Banning Gold Exports

Zhao Jinqing, Director of the Industry and Commerce Department's Shanghai Office, to address the issue of declining silver prices, previously invited business leaders from China, Britain, the United States, and other countries in Shanghai last Wednesday to a meeting for discussion and to seek opinions for adoption by the National Government and submission to the League of Nations. Yesterday afternoon, Zhao invited leaders of French, Japanese, German, and Italian commercial organizations in Shanghai for a second informal exchange of views at the Industry and Commerce Department's Shanghai Office in the Jianghai Customs Building. Those present included Mr. Dubosq, President of the French Chamber of Commerce; Mr. Miri, President of the Japanese Chamber of Commerce; Mr. Vogel, President of the German Chamber of Commerce; Mr. Fumagalli, President of the Italian Chamber of Commerce; Mr. Tsuchiya, President of Mitsui Bank; Mr. Hirtz, President of Banque de l'Indochine; Mr. Last, President of Deutsch-Asiatische Bank; Mr. Hattori, President of the Bank of Chosen; Mr. Charlotte, Manager of Arnhold Trading Company; and from the Chinese side, Zhao Jinqing, Zhu Chengzhang, Xia Jinlin, Qin Runqing, Lin Kanghou, Hu Xiansheng, Shou Jingwei, Zhang Xianglin, Gao Lu, Li Weimin, and over ten others. After approximately two hours of exchanging opinions, the main points of each party can be summarized into three: (1) the suggestion of Mitsui Bank's Tsuchiya; (2) requesting the governments of India and Annam to temporarily suspend the sale of silver to China for a period of two years; (3) the National Government should order customs to prohibit the export of cash; (4) the German and French proposal to maintain peace and restore domestic transportation. The details are as follows:

Zhao Jinqing stated in his address: "Today we are discussing the silver price problem. I am extremely delighted that you gentlemen have graced us with your presence. As leaders of French, Japanese, German, and Italian commercial organizations in Shanghai, your willingness to come is appreciated, and I trust you will provide valuable guidance. Recently, silver prices have fallen again, and the resulting impact will inevitably lead to a continued increase in commodity prices. This will impede China's import trade on the one hand, and have a very negative impact on export commerce on the other. Both Chinese and foreign merchants are suffering. Therefore, the low silver price has become an international problem. Low silver prices are not only a major obstacle to the development of Chinese industry and commerce, but also severely harm international trade. The government is currently planning to implement various measures, but this matter is of great importance and requires collective wisdom and broad consultation. We have convened this informal meeting to discuss various relief methods, hoping to contribute something that the government can adopt and implement. Last Wednesday, business leaders from China, Britain, and the United States also gathered for a similar discussion. Today, I hope that you gentlemen will express your views as much as possible."

Opinions from All Parties: After Zhao Jinqing's speech, the business representatives from various countries present expressed their opinions. The suggestion from Mr. Tsuchiya, President of Mitsui Bank, was the most specific. Mr. Tsuchiya's suggestion was, in brief: to alleviate the preciousness of gold and the cheapness of silver, the first step is to ban gold exports. This measure has been implemented in various European and American countries in the past. Even in Japan, it was implemented for fifteen years before being lifted recently. Because China has very little cash reserves, if exports are prohibited, there will be no need to purchase foreign exchange for gold, and the price of gold will naturally fall, while the price of silver will rise. Some say that gold trading in Shanghai is all about selling short and buying long, and that there is no real trading in gold bars. However, last Saturday, 10,000 gold pounds were exported, and this amount is not small. Secondly, the National Government can consult with major silver countries, such as Annam and India, to ensure that they do not sell silver to China for two years. Qin Runqing, President of the China Reclamation Bank, said that the paper currency issued by various banks in Shanghai totals 200 million yuan. If a reserve of 60% is maintained as required, then 120 million yuan in silver is needed. Shanghai has a total of 200 million yuan in silver, which is not much. Mr. Hirtz, President of Banque de l'Indochine, and other French, German, and Italian figures argued that artificial methods are insufficient to alleviate the trend of expensive gold and cheap silver. The fundamental solution lies in China maintaining peace and quickly restoring national transportation so that the silver stored in Shanghai can circulate. According to some sources, once the silver stored in Shanghai circulates inland, foreign silver will inevitably flood in. Even from Annam alone, there are 20 million yuan in silver currency, of which 7 million yuan has already been imported into China, and the rest is waiting for an opportunity to be imported into China. The National Government's order to prohibit the import of silver coins into China is also for this reason.

Li Fusun's Opinions on the Decline in Silver Prices 143

Reporters from various newspapers specifically sought the opinion of Mr. Li Fusun on the matter of the decline in silver prices. Mr. Li is the Chairman of the Bank of China and is very knowledgeable in economics and experienced in commerce. His remarks are recorded below:

Mr. Li said, "The current low silver price is largely due to international reasons, which we cannot control. However, there is an important point, which is that due to the low silver price, there is panic in Shanghai, and its impact extends to other markets internationally. In my opinion, panic is not necessary. The main reasons for the recent decline in silver prices are two: (1) The currency system of Indochina has changed from a pure silver standard to a virtual gold standard, which was completed at the end of January of this year. The method is to convert all the silver reserves of the Banque de l'Indochine (the sole issuer of banknotes) into gold reserves within six months, requiring approximately 5 to 6 million pounds of gold, mostly purchased from the Shanghai market. (2) After adopting the gold standard, the Indian financial authorities have repeatedly secretly sold the silver obtained from melting coins in the London market. Their sales are neither at a fixed time nor at a fixed price, and their attitude is very difficult to grasp. Outsiders often exaggerate their words, occasionally causing panic in the market. The above two are the so-called international reasons. However, these two reasons have already affected the silver market in the past, so if no other reasons occur, the current low silver price can be said to have reached its limit, or is not far from its limit. At this time, we should regard it as a period of recovery, not a period of panic. Those who discuss the silver market today often fail to consider that Shanghai is the storage place for the nation's silver reserves. It must be known that the silver stored in Shanghai is not purely the silver stored in Shanghai alone; it actually includes the silver reserves for the banknotes circulating in this port and the country. If industry develops in the future, commerce and goods sell well, and the amount of banknotes issued increases, then this silver reserve will also increase. Banknotes are merely representatives of silver. Issuing banknotes requires storing a considerable amount of cash for redemption. Therefore, the large amount of silver stored in Shanghai should not affect the silver market and cause its price to fall. Most of the silver stored there is actually no different from being stored inland. It is a mistake to base discussions of the silver market solely on the statistics of silver stored in Shanghai, without considering that this stored silver is a banknote reserve or goods for sale. As for why large amounts of silver are concentrated in Shanghai, it is because the situation has not yet stabilized. Historically, when military events occur, Shanghai has been the nation's silver treasury. In the future, when peace lasts a little longer, the silver will inevitably disperse inland, and the banks in the major ports that now deposit silver reserves in Shanghai will at that time convert some of it to be stored in their respective locations, no longer concentrated in Shanghai. In addition, there is also a common misconception that if our country adopts the gold standard, the use of silver in our country will inevitably decrease. Regarding this issue, it can be discussed from the following two points: (1) At this time, it is not easy for our country to suddenly change from the silver standard to the gold standard. In my opinion, it should be done when the situation is more favorable than it is now. However, before I see the report of the Kemmerer Financial Advisory Group, I am unable to make a final conclusion. (2) Minister of Finance Song stated that even if China adopts the gold standard, the currency in the country will not be gold coins but still silver coins, indicating that although our country's currency system may be improved, the use of silver in the country will not be greatly reduced. I am saying this because I do not want to give the impression that I want to control the market situation. This is definitely beyond my ability, because the Shanghai silver market is governed by economic principles and political reasons, and will never be swayed by any optimistic remarks. However, it is my wish that we should try to use common sense to restore the market situation and not be moved by rumors. Over the years, the silver market in Shanghai has been loose, and the capital available for productive enterprises is more abundant than ever before. If merchants can take advantage of the opportunity and devote themselves to productive enterprises, then what they do is in line with economic principles. On the one hand, politically, I also hope that the government will quickly promulgate laws to protect industry and commerce to promote their progress, and the silver market will naturally return to calm. In short, instead of focusing on strategies to save the silver market, it is better to shift your gaze and skills to the restoration of economic order and the development of industry and commerce, so that the demand for silver coins increases and the value of silver naturally rises."

Changes in the City's Population in 1929 145

Household Increase of 30,976 Households

Population Increase of 120,595 People

Since the population census, the city's Public Security Bureau has compiled a monthly statistical table of changes for reference. The population changes for 1929 are recorded below. January: 1,506,190 people, 310,809 households; February: 1,499,592 people, 310,849 households; March: 1,504,024 people, 311,965 households; April: 1,509,963 people, 313,526 households; May: 1,513,874 people, 314,839 households; June: 1,525,562 people, 318,629 households; July: 1,547,384 people, 324,586 households; August: 1,559,671 people, 327,978 households; September: 1,573,833 people, 331,554 households; October: 1,591,517 people, 335,546 households; November: 1,609,663 people, 339,627 households; December: 1,620,187 people, 341,785 households.

It is reported that the number of households in December 1928 was 313,14. The difference between the increase and decrease in the number of households for the whole year was the sharpest decrease in the number of households in January, and the decrease in the population was the lowest in January and February. After that, it gradually increased, with the largest increase rate in July. According to the bureau's investigation, the main reasons for the increase or decrease, in addition to the fact that the number of households changed in January had just been investigated in the previous year and had not been re-investigated, and the reason was unknown, most of the decrease in the population was due to death exceeding birth, in addition to the decrease in household migration. The main reasons for the monthly increase after February are that municipal facilities are becoming more and more perfect, and public security administration is also actively reorganized. Residents have generally obtained security guarantees and welfare increases, so more and more people are moving into the city.

Procedures for Applying for Loss of Nationality 146

Personnel Should Be Dispatched for Investigation

The Shanghai Special Municipal Government yesterday issued an order to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, stating: "In order to comply with the matter, according to the Ministry of Interior's inquiry, after investigating the matter of people applying for loss of nationality, in accordance with the provisions of Article 12 of the Nationality Law, the Ministry of Interior shall not permit the loss of nationality if one of the following circumstances exists: (1) Having reached the age of military service, not being exempt from military service obligations, and not yet having performed military service; (2) Currently serving in the military; (3) Currently holding a Chinese civil or military position. Furthermore, according to the provisions of Article 13 of the same law, even if one meets the provisions of Article 12 of the same law, one shall still not lose nationality if one of the following circumstances exists: (1) Being a criminal suspect or defendant; (2) Having been sentenced and the execution has not yet ended; (3) Being a civil defendant; (4) The compulsory execution has not yet ended; (5) Having been declared bankrupt and not yet reinstated; (6) Having overdue taxes or having been subject to overdue tax penalties that have not yet ended. Furthermore, according to the provisions of Article 14 of the same law, those who lose nationality lose the rights that non-Chinese people cannot enjoy. If a person who loses nationality has enjoyed the aforementioned rights before losing nationality, if they do not transfer them to a Chinese person within one year after losing nationality, the rights shall belong to the national treasury. The original intention was to prevent people from attempting to evade obligations by losing nationality. The Ministry previously issued application forms and stipulated that whether the person applying for loss of nationality has any of the circumstances in Article 12 or Article 13 of the Nationality Law, and whether they have any rights that should be lost under Article 14 of the same law, should be indicated separately in the application form for verification. In the future, regarding cases of people applying for loss of nationality, the competent local official office or embassy should urgently dispatch appropriate personnel to local courts and chambers of commerce to thoroughly investigate and order them to obtain a guarantee letter from two or more reputable shops established by Chinese people in the Chinese place of residence, and after the reviewing agency has reviewed it and found no discrepancies, it should be sent to the Ministry of Interior for verification with a truthful endorsement, so as to ensure prudence and prevent fraud. In addition to distributing the information, we are also consulting your government to investigate and instruct your subordinates to comply with the handling, etc. With this approval, we order the bureau to comply with the handling. This order."

International Opium Suppression Investigators Arrive in Shanghai 151

A Group of Four

Wen Hui Bao reported that the commission of the League of Nations investigating the opium situation in the Far East, after investigating Burma, British Malaya, the Dutch East Indies, Siam, Hong Kong, and other places, arrived in Shanghai yesterday (16th). The whole group consists of four people, with Axel Ekstrand, the Swedish Minister to Argentina, as the director, and Charles Kittar, the President of the Belgian Political and Economic Association, and Dr. Halaša, the former Czechoslovak Minister to Brazil, as members. Leng Bo, an official of the League of Nations Secretariat, is the accompanying secretary. It is reported that the French Concession authorities have already treated them well.

This Year's Progress in Opium Suppression in the City 152

The Municipal Public Security Bureau lists and reports on opium suppression to the Municipal Government and the Opium Suppression Committee on a regular basis for performance evaluation. It is reported that the bureau has listed and submitted the progress of opium suppression in the first half of this year, from July to the end of the year of 1929, for verification and transfer. In summary, the bureau's opium suppression work, all matters related to the examination of public officials' regulations, still refer to the chapters and regulations for the affiliated officials and police, who are responsible for reporting. For several months, strict examinations have been conducted, and no suspicious points have been found. In fact, it has been effective. However, the elimination of drug atmosphere is the first to stop trafficking, and the two Chinese and French concessions in Shanghai are adjacent to each other, with convenient transportation in all directions, making prevention difficult. The bureau has repeatedly ordered the land and water police teams to seriously investigate at railway stations, harbors, land and water ports, and at the junction of the Chinese and French concessions. In addition, recently, traitors and rioters have often lured rural women to carry smuggled opium and guns, hoping to smuggle them. The bureau immediately recruited female inspectors and distributed them to various districts and offices to carry out inspections, which was quite fruitful, especially in the 5th and 2nd districts of the water patrol team, where more trafficking cases were detected. There were often more than 20 cases of opium seized in a month. The bureau has reported the cases separately, and rewarded those who have contributed to encourage them. As for the prohibition of smoking, opening lights for sale and smoking has long been strictly prohibited, but those who have been deeply infected with the habit of smoking privately are still unavoidable. Every time the bureau cracks a case, the perpetrators are dealt with according to the severity of their crimes, and are transferred to the court along with the evidence for legal action. The effect of opium suppression in each district office is listed and reported at the end of the month, and is carefully assessed and punished or rewarded as appropriate. In the first half of the year, the bureau handled a total of 1,104 cases of trafficking, selling, and smoking opium, an increase of 389 cases compared with the first half of the year. More than 48,000 taels of miscellaneous opium and opium paste were seized, and more than 520 boxes of red pills and morphine were seized, almost an increase of four-fifths compared with the previous half year. The reason for this is that although it is caused by the serious investigation of the various districts and teams, it is also because of the recent unrest in the local area, increased unemployment, and the rush of dangerous people to gather together, regardless of violating the law, and secretly plotting to sell for profit. Once strictly investigated and banned, all of them were cracked down. This is the actual situation of the increase in opium cases.

Two Organizations Request Negotiations on Japanese Harsh Taxes Again 153

The China National Goods Maintenance Association and the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Joint Association sent a telegram to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce yesterday, stating: "We have investigated that our country's gauze and satin are sold to Japan, South Korea, and other places in large numbers. In the autumn of 1924, the Japanese government suddenly designated our country's silk as a luxury item and imposed a heavy tax of 100% of the value, resulting in the disappearance of goods for the past six or seven years. The losses of the silk industry are more than several million. The unemployed industry and commerce have not been able to obtain relief. Our associations have been appealing for years and sending telegrams back and forth, but it is difficult to bet on effectiveness. Fortunately, now is the time to start revising the Sino-Japanese treaty. We beg your government, court, and departments to consider that this matter is related to the national economy and people's livelihood, and is a very important issue that should be addressed in advance. If they do not agree, please ask the national government to immediately implement the same tax rate on foreign goods coming to China to show equality and save the people's livelihood. We cannot bear the urgency of our prayers. Respectfully, the China National Goods Maintenance Association and the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Joint Association."

Regarding the Petition to Cancel the Autumn Cocoon Silk Tax 155

Huang Jin Shen, Chairman of the General Silk and Cocoon Association Committee of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, submitted a request yesterday to the finance department.

It concerns the matter of autumn cocoons being exempt from tax and a request to cancel the silk tax, which was instructed on October 10 of the previous year in document number three: "Upon reviewing the received documents, including the telegram from the Yiyang Association (omitted portion), you are to comply accordingly." Upon receiving this instruction, and noting that over four months have passed without knowing whether Zhejiang province has implemented any improved measures or replied to Suzhou, we have been waiting anxiously. The association has carefully translated the sections of the instruction and must urgently make the following clarifications regarding the facts: (1) Exempting cocoon tax without exempting silk tax. In Suzhou province, only the monthly cocoon tax has been levied on local silk cocoons; there is no silk tax. Each hundred catties of dry cocoons from various cocoon-producing counties are subject to a cocoon tax of twelve yuan and forty cents. Even Wuxi county reports and pays taxes based on the amount of silk reeled from cocoons, not as a silk tax. This is the case for spring cocoons, let alone autumn cocoons. Therefore, the autumn cocoon silk tax should be canceled. (2) Exempting the autumn cocoon tax is to show consideration for silkworm farmers, not to favor capital factories. Autumn silkworm rearing is not initiated by silkworm farmers themselves; silk cocoon merchants produce autumn seeds and distribute them to the farmers. Significant expenses are incurred in setting up cold storage facilities during the seed production stage, and generous cocoon prices are offered after the cocoons are harvested to encourage farmers, all to increase production and compensate for the insufficient spring silkworm yield. Therefore, merchants play a proactive role in the development of autumn cocoons, while silkworm farmers are reactive. The Zhejiang province measures may misunderstand the source of autumn seeds by only considering silkworm farmers. Silk cocoon merchants deserve to share the preferential treatment with the diligent silkworm farmers for their painstaking efforts in autumn seed production. Therefore, the autumn cocoon silk tax should be canceled for this reason as well. (3) Tax exemption for inland areas is already a concession. Silk factories in treaty ports, some of which are established by foreigners, enjoy the benefit of tax exemption, while inland silk factories, which are purely Chinese-owned, are not. This preferential treatment of foreigners over Chinese is a flawed perspective in Zhejiang province, and such measures can easily lead to malpractices. Japan, being a strong competitor in raw silk, faces a shortage of raw materials and relies on purchasing fresh cocoons from China. The autumn seeds painstakingly developed by our silk merchants are used to supply raw materials to foreigners, with tax-free direct exports. In essence, the efforts of silk merchants and the diligence of silkworm farmers are benefiting others. The government would surely not want to adopt such a strategy. Therefore, the autumn cocoon silk tax should be canceled for this reason as well. (4) Silk reeled from silk factories in treaty ports and transported to inland areas is also subject to tax. Silk factories generally produce raw silk for export trade, unlike native silk. All silk products from treaty ports are declared and shipped out locally; there is no reason to transport them to inland areas. The fourth provision of the original measure becomes redundant if the sales channels of factory silk are clear. As for inland silk factories, their monthly output cannot be exported without being transported to treaty ports. Therefore, the tax exemption is merely a verbal promise, creating a new silk tax under the guise of exempting cocoon tax. Although explanations are provided, they only create more doubts. Therefore, the autumn cocoon silk tax should be canceled for this reason as well. In summary, regarding the fundamental aspects of this matter: (1) It must be understood that there is no silk tax in inland areas, only a cocoon tax. Once the cocoon tax is exempted, there is no silk tax to speak of. (2) It must be understood that factory silk is sold to Europe and America through treaty ports, and there is no reason to transport it to inland areas, so there is no silk tax to collect. If the government considers these two points, it will understand that the repeated requests are not unfounded complaints. The development of autumn cocoons is only two years old, and both Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have seen positive results, with Wuxi county in particular demonstrating high yields. In the future, with sufficient seed production, the output will be no less than that of spring cocoons. If this opaque and fragmented approach is adopted, it will lead to significant malpractices, being lenient towards treaty ports and harsh towards inland areas, akin to driving fish into the depths, granting foreigners the benefit of absorbing raw materials. The hard work of silk merchants in seed production and the diligence of silkworm farmers will instead be used to supply the deficiencies of strong neighbors. Why then bother with such active promotion? The unresolved case has been pending for over half a year, and autumn seed production must soon be prepared. Unless the original measures are thoroughly changed and the previously unheard-of silk tax is completely canceled, the government's intention to promote autumn cocoons will be counterproductive. Industry is the foundation of the country, and the government and merchants are closely intertwined. Matters of the day should be clarified promptly. We earnestly request your acceptance of the above points and the fundamental cancellation of the autumn cocoon silk tax, as well as a thorough improvement of the original tax exemption measures to eliminate obstacles and maintain the silk industry for the public good.

Compilation of Commemorative Week Activities in Various Institutions 156

The Municipal Executive Committee held its 47th Sun Yat-sen Commemorative Week yesterday at 9:30 AM. Over 200 attendees included members of the Executive and Supervisory Committees, along with guests. Those who consider themselves revolutionaries, whether they are party members or work in political institutions or the military under party rule, must first have these virtues. To have these virtues, they must possess the following four spirits: (1) serving the public, (2) determination to sacrifice, (3) unity and love, and (4) strict adherence to discipline. The repeated betrayals of the nation, the inability to eradicate corruption and evil, and the inevitable problems of disorganization and inefficiency in various institutions are all due to revolutionaries not understanding the morality they should have. Over 1.8 Billion Yuan

(2) Banking groups: 256,332,000 yuan. (3) Textile industry: 250,064,500 yuan. (4) Agriculture, forestry, and mining: 206,695,000 yuan. (5) General trade: 162,860,000 yuan. (6) Manufacturing: 144,494,100 yuan. (7) Electricity industry: 47,211,100 yuan. (8) Civil engineering: 31,708,000 yuan. (9) Other: 58,610,000 yuan. The total is 1,809,154,400 yuan. The following is a detailed breakdown by region: Dalian: 700,309,300 yuan; Shanghai: 274,005,200 yuan; Qingdao: 139,645,000 yuan; Fengtian: 50,120,400 yuan; Hankou: 40,040,760 yuan; Tianjin: 35,963,000 yuan; Beiping: 7,178,000 yuan; Other: 500,177,160 yuan.

The China National Products Maintenance Association Cables for Support of the Nanyang Tobacco Factory 158

The China National Products Maintenance Association considers the continuous losses of the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company and the cessation of factory operations a major blow to the future of the national products industry. The Executive Committee resolved to cable the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting substantial support and assistance to revive the business, so that factory operations can continue to develop and workers will not lose their jobs. The original telegram is as follows: "We have recently heard that the Shanghai factory of Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Co., Ltd. has suffered from various environmental pressures in recent years, incurring significant losses and unable to sustain itself, leading to the suspension of operations and closure of the factory. Upon learning this news, we are shocked and dismayed. We believe that this company is a giant in China's tobacco industry. Over the years, it has received support from the people of the country, and its business has flourished throughout the country, initially helping to recover some of the huge annual losses in the industry. However, compared with foreign merchants, it still feels financially weak and lagging behind. Unfortunately, it has recently been hit by frequent labor unrest and heavy taxes, leading to a rapid decline in business. Now it is unable to maintain operations and has even closed down. Not only are the company's years of hard work and dedication wasted, but the thousands of workers who depend on it for a living, as well as the promising future of China's tobacco industry, are also cut off. Thinking of this, we deeply regret the future of national products. Moreover, at a time when the gold price crisis is raging, our government is making painstaking efforts to provide relief, with clear statements on developing industry, using national products, increasing production, and reducing taxes on national products. The people of the country are deeply gratified, but we never expected that Shanghai's leading industrial factory would be forced to sacrifice under the constraints of a severe environment. This runs counter to the intentions of our government and is completely different. Our association, being a national product group, and at this critical juncture for the survival of the national products industry, dares to offer our humble opinion, hoping to be accepted. We believe that although the Nanyang Tobacco Company is only in the tobacco industry, it is of great importance to the future of national products, people's livelihood, and the national economy. At this time of factory closure and suspension of operations, we earnestly request your departments, governments, and courts to allocate funds to maintain and continue operations, and to lift the heavy taxes imposed in recent years, in order to restore the original tax situation of three years ago. At the same time, please increase the import tariffs on foreign tobacco and implement a production tax on products manufactured by foreign merchants in China, in order to implement a policy of protecting national products trade and to comply with the Premier's legacy on people's livelihood. This is what our association urgently presents and appeals for adoption and implementation, in order to provide relief. We are extremely anxious and cannot express all our thoughts. We await your instructions. China National Products Maintenance Association Standing Committee Members Wang Jiean, Wang Xingyi, and Wang Hanqiang respectfully kowtow."

Continued News on the Sino-U.S. Shipping 160

Lack of Silk for Shipment to the United States. Since the reduction of freight charges for Chinese silk on Pacific liners, most of the silk stored in Shanghai has been rushed to the United States within the past two weeks. Recently, the port has shown a shortage of silk for export. The reason is that various silk factories in Shanghai have been shut down for a long time, resulting in a minimal amount of goods being shipped, which has delayed delivery and affected exports. According to various shipping companies, it will take about three to four weeks before silk can be loaded, and operations are currently at a standstill.

New York Reduces Freight Charges. Various shipping companies on the Sino-U.S. New York route have invited representatives from all shipping companies to discuss competitive business methods in response to the Japanese shipping lines' excessive reduction of freight rates. Except for the freight charges for Zhejiang silk, which will be discussed separately, the export freight rates for all other goods have been reduced uniformly starting yesterday (17th), with a further 20% reduction on the already reduced rates to enhance competitiveness. For example, mineral sand has been reduced from 10 yuan to 8 yuan per ton, pig bristles from 20 yuan to 16 yuan, wool from 12 yuan to 10 yuan, leather from 10 yuan to 7.5 yuan, duck feathers from 14.5 yuan to 11.5 yuan, cotton yarn from 10 yuan to 8 yuan, eggs from 15 yuan to 12 yuan, and rhubarb from 15 yuan to 12 yuan. For goods not listed in the designated freight rate list, the rate has been reduced from 15 yuan to 14 yuan. Yesterday, the union has notified all customers that the rate is collected in US dollars, with each ton occupying 40 cubic feet or weighing 2,240 pounds, and the standard is applicable to ships traveling through the Panama Canal.

Inaugural Meeting of the Shanghai-Ningbo New Steamer 161

Ningbo commercial organizations are opposing the four companies on the Shanghai-Ningbo route increasing freight charges. They have submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to stop the increase and are discussing the establishment of a new Shanghai-Ningbo steamer company to fundamentally resolve the issue. At the end of last month, a meeting was held to determine the establishment cost to be 500,000 yuan, divided into 100,000 shares, with the initial purchase of a steamer to operate between Shanghai and Ningbo. In order to expedite the establishment, Ningbo merchants in Shanghai have been notified to attend the inaugural meeting of the Shanghai-Ningbo New Steamer in Ningbo on the 18th to discuss fundraising, share collection, and ship purchase procedures. It is planned to start operations within three months.

Disaster Report from Yuhuan, Eastern Zhejiang 162

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Association received a telegram from the Yuhuan County Chamber of Commerce yesterday: "Yuhuan County is experiencing an unprecedented disaster in 200 years. Pests, floods, wind, and drought have struck successively, leaving the land barren with nothing remaining. Grain prices have soared, and reserves are exhausted. Even wealthy households are on the verge of bankruptcy. The people are extremely distressed and displaced, with over 50,000 suffering from the disaster. With continuous rain and snow since winter for two months, wheat roots have rotted and the spring harvest is hopeless. Fishermen cannot fish, making livelihoods even more difficult. To this day, children are being sold, and people are fleeing. Seaweed and mountain herbs are being used as food. Some are even digging up sticky soil to prolong their lives, leading to digestive blockages and death from poisoning. The number of such cases is countless. Desperate famine victims are gathering in crowds, causing disturbances almost daily. The disaster area is vast, and the future is uncertain. If significant funds are not allocated promptly for relief, we fear that half of the 160,000 people will starve to death, and there will be no clean land in the 700 square li. We humbly request the immediate allocation of 100,000 yuan for spring relief and 20,000 sets of cotton clothing to save those who are groaning and waiting to die. Yuhuan County Chamber of Commerce Chairman Lin Wenhan and others respectfully kowtow." Also, the Yuhuan County Tonglin Lichun Committee reported: "Thousands of families in the Tonglin area and our village rely entirely on farming for a living. Unexpectedly, in June and July of last year, locusts and pests devoured everything, and strong winds and floods caused disasters one after another. The early and late rice crops planted were turned into weeds, resulting in no harvest of grain. From August to November, there was a prolonged drought with no rain, and the harvest of sweet potatoes, rice, and sweet potato vermicelli was less than 20%. This is a famine year unlike any in ancient times. Moreover, our area is inherently poor, leading to starvation and cold, with people hanging themselves, drowning themselves, and dying of illness due to starvation. All sorts of things have happened. Previously, we received 500 yuan from the provincial government for emergency relief, temporarily alleviating the immediate crisis, but it was only a drop in the bucket, unable to cover the entire area. Currently, our area and our village are about to run out of food, with no way to make a living. We will inevitably face starvation and death everywhere, a heartbreaking and tragic sight beyond words. We humbly request you to make every effort to convert funds into rice and quickly send it to our area to feed the starving people, so that there will be no more starvation and suicides. All of this will be your act of re-creation. Yuhuan County Tonglin District Poor People's Representative Gan Wufu and others."

Page 15

Local News Two

News Report Editor Xu Yusun Dies Tragically 170

The Plight of Newspaper Reporters

Unable to Return Home Before Late at Night

Xu Yusun Meets Tragic End in Robbery

Shot Once, Giving His Life

At approximately 12 a.m. yesterday, Xu Yusun, a native of Zhenjiang and economic news editor at the News Report newspaper, was robbed and fatally shot while walking on Route Paul Brunat (now Huaihai Road) in the French Concession, inside the Sanyi Lane. The details are as follows:

Brief Biography of the Xu Family: Xu Yusun was 33 years old, originally from the Shunjangzhou area across from Dagang Town, Zhenjiang. His family had moved to Shanghai years ago. His father, Wei Liu, was in the lumber business and passed away ten years ago. His mother, Zhang, is currently sixty years old. His wife, Chen, is the same age as him. He has four siblings; he is the second eldest. His elder brother, Fansun, is already over forty and works as a clerk at the Banking Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road. His third brother, Shuchu, is 21 years old, and his fourth brother, Fuchu, is 19. Both are currently students at the Yucai School at the Datongmen in the southern part of the city. During the day, Xu worked as an editor for the Banking Weekly at No. 4 Hong Kong Road and also served as a secretary in the office of the President of the Central Bank. He went to the News Report newspaper to work in the evenings, working tirelessly with hardly any time for rest. He had three sons: the eldest, Zengdi, is 12 years old; the second, Yingkui, is 7 years old; and the youngest, Zengyi, is only 3 years old. Xu initially studied at the Nantong Textile Institute and later graduated from the Nanyang Commercial College in Shanghai. He had reportedly worked at the News Report newspaper for nine years.

Death During Robbery on the Way Home: The Xu family resides at No. 23 Tingyun Lane on Route Francis Garnier (now Kangping Road) in the French Concession. His elder brother, Fansun, rents part of No. 22 next door to live separately because the family home is small and crowded. Xu returned home from the newspaper office every day no earlier than midnight. The day before the incident, when Xu left home, he told his mother that he planned to return home early, no later than midnight. That evening, at approximately 11 p.m., Xu finished his work and started home. However, while walking inside Sanyi Lane on Route Paul Brunat in the French Concession, less than a few paces from his back door, several robbers suddenly rushed out from the darkness and stopped him to rob him. At the time, the robbers had already stripped off his black cat fur coat and mandarin jacket and were about to flee the lane when Xu shouted for help. The robbers then turned back and shot at Xu. One bullet struck his left flank, piercing through to his right back, and he immediately fell to the ground and died. The robbers fled in the chaos. However, no one heard the alarm at the time. It wasn't until 12:30 a.m., when the doorman of Sanyi Lane went out to close the iron gate at the entrance of the lane, that he noticed the body. However, he did not recognize Xu, so he immediately reported it to the police station.

Body Taken to Hall for Examination: After receiving the report, the police chief immediately ordered detectives to investigate. They found a bullet casing in the lane. The deceased was found wearing a short jacket, cotton trousers, leather shoes, and a felt hat, with nothing else on him. Later, several cards were found in the lane. The patrolman was about to take the cards, which had occupations, names, and addresses on them, to Tingyun Lane to inquire, when at the same time, Xu's mother was leaning against her pillow, hoping for her beloved son to return, as he was late. Suddenly, she heard a commotion outside the door and knew something was wrong. She got up and went outside, only to see her beloved son lying stiff in a pool of blood. Xu's mother wept bitterly over the body, and all the family members gathered upon hearing the news. They helped Xu's mother back inside and took the body to the Tongren Fuyuantang coroner's office. Yesterday, the Criminal Division of the police station ordered detectives to notify the deceased's brother, Xu Fansun, to come to the office to report the case. Judge Zhu of the French Court arrived at the office at 3 p.m. to conduct an examination. After the patrolman reported the details, Judge Zhu declared that the deceased had been fatally shot by robbers and that the family should be allowed to prepare a coffin and collect the body, pending the police's rigorous pursuit and investigation of the robbers. After the examination, Xu's third brother, Shuchu, hired undertakers to transport the body in a hearse to the Jingjiang Guild Hall in the Old West Gate for encoffining, and the body will be sent back to his hometown for burial on a selected date.

Huo Shouhua's Lawsuit Against Wen and Guo Ruled on Yesterday 171

Wen and Guo Declared Not Guilty

Elements of Defamation Not Met

The Guangzhao Guild Hall's address on Ningbo Road in the International Settlement was leased by the guild hall to the Shanghai Bank to build a large building. However, Huo Shouhua, the chairman of the Guangdong Club, which was previously affiliated with the Guangzhao Guild Hall, and Wen Zongyao and Guo Biao, directors of the company, had disagreements over this issue. On December 24th of last year, the board of directors of the Guangzhao Guild Hall issued a leaflet announcing the situation to fellow villagers from the Guangzhao region residing in Shanghai. Huo Shouhua believed that the leaflet contained language that damaged his personal reputation. He hired a lawyer to file a private prosecution with the Provisional Court, requesting that Wen Zongyao (styled Qinpu) and Guo Biao be brought to court and punished according to Articles 324 and 325 of the Criminal Code, and that they be ordered to publish an apology in the newspaper. The case had already been heard once. Yesterday morning, Chief Justice Xu Jiashi opened the Seventh Court and summoned witnesses to continue the hearing. First, Luo Qin'san testified that the club had requested the guild hall to negotiate with the Shanghai Bank because the guild hall had leased the address to the Shanghai Bank to build a new building, and the contract did not specify a location for the guild hall's office or allow the guild hall's plaque to remain displayed. Therefore, a family reunion meeting was held to resolve this issue. Next, a witness surnamed Kuang testified that he attended the family reunion meeting as a guest and personally heard Huo Shouhua say that the club should supervise the guild hall. Huo immediately argued that he did not see this witness present at the time and did not know him. The two sides questioned each other and swore to the heavens. Later, Huo stated that his remarks at the time did not say that the Guangdong Club would supervise the Guangzhao Guild Hall. However, the leaflet issued by the defendant accused me of seizing and occupying, which is the behavior of local tyrants and bullies. If I, Huo, had such behavior, I would accept the punishment of a local tyrant. The defendant slandered me with such words, making it impossible for me to live in society. Therefore, I have no choice but to seek legal protection, and so on. Chief Justice presided. Next, the defendant Wen Zongyao testified that the leaflet said that Huo had the intention of seizing and occupying, and his letters of February 19th and March 1st revealed his intention to occupy. He wanted to stop the construction of the new building in order to stay in the old building for a long time. Wen also answered the plaintiff's lawyer's question, stating that the Shanghai Bank leased the land to the Guangzhao Guild Hall to build a building. The guild hall's board of directors appointed me, Chen Bingqian, Guo Biao, Guo Le, and others on August 24th of the year before last to negotiate with the Shanghai Bank. The agreement was reached on December 25th, and the contract was submitted to Chairman Tang Shaochuan for review. The board of directors then held a meeting to review the contract item by item. As a result of the discussion, the entire contract was passed. The bank now retains 5,200 square feet of land for the guild hall's use, but the bank is unwilling to lease it to the club for use as an office, and so on. Huang Hongjun, a director of the club, also testified and was critical of the contract between the company and the bank and sympathetic to Huo Shouhua's actions at the time. The witness Chen Bingqian also stated that Huo did say at the family reunion meeting that the club should supervise the guild hall. Finally, the lawyers for both sides began their arguments. The arguments ended at 2 p.m., and Chief Justice Xu then ruled that the defendants Wen Qinpu and Guo Biao were not guilty and announced the reasons for the ruling, stating that Wen Qinpu proposed at the board of directors meeting of the guild hall on December 24th that if the leaflet issued by the preparatory committee of the Guangdong Fellow Villagers Association was not clarified, fellow villagers from Guangzhao residing in Shanghai might have misunderstandings. The true situation of the land lease should be printed and announced so that fellow villagers would be aware. The purpose of issuing the notice was to defend and explain, not to spread the plaintiff's evil deeds to the public. Examining the contents of the notice, it is clear that it contains language debating right and wrong. The facts pointed out were merely that the plaintiff had requested to lease back the base for the Guangdong Club and was unsuccessful, and that he was obstructing the project out of resentment. The plaintiff was said to have contributed to the Guangdong Club, which shows that the plaintiff's protest was a matter of public concern and not an attempt to seize and occupy for personal gain. It cannot be said that the plaintiff's evil deeds and scandals, that is, the matters pointed out, are sufficient to affect the plaintiff's social standing and there is no risk of loss of reputation. The elements of the crime of defamation are not met, and the defendants are not guilty. Upon hearing the ruling, both parties left, and the case ended there.

French Municipal Council Accused 172

Plaintiff: Sino-French Company

Consular Court Opens Trial

According to the Continental Daily, on December 30th, thieves broke into the Sino-French Company at No. 693 Xujiahui Road and stole part of the staff's wages, totaling 4,600 yuan. Afterward, the Sino-French Company accused the French Municipal Council of negligence of duty by the police and claimed that it could provide sufficient evidence. The French Consular Court summoned both parties and opened the trial on the 13th of this month. The plaintiff's lawyer, Mo Tiyi, first refuted the defendant's lawyer Ba He's argument that the Administrative Committee of the Municipal Council was not responsible for the actions of the police, stating that since there was no judicial police force in the concession, all the police officers should be considered municipal police officers, and the Municipal Council should be responsible for the police affairs it handles. If the court accepts this principle and responsibility, then he can easily prove the police's dereliction of duty based on the subsequent investigation, so the Sino-French Company should demand compensation, and so on. Lawyer Ba He argued that the Municipal Council only provided the necessary expenses for handling police affairs to several responsible personnel to handle police affairs and refuted the plaintiff's lawyer's points, saying that if the court accepts his principle, then the Municipal Council will be responsible for every petty theft that occurs in the concession. Subsequently, the lawyers on both sides displayed their eloquence and debated for a long time. The court then announced a recess and scheduled a date for the verdict. It is said that this type of case may still be the first time in the French Court, so its outcome is of great concern to all parties.

Spring Grazing of Sheep Hinders Farming 175

Wusong City Committee Petitions for Issuance of Proclamation Banning

In the Bao Shan County territory, it has been the custom that, every spring, the county government issues a proclamation to all county residents banning sheep grazing to avoid damage to crops. Violators will be severely punished according to law. Therefore, farmers in the county invariably transport their livestock to other counties to sell during this period, and the value of sheep is therefore lower than usual. This spring, the Bao Shan County government again issued a proclamation banning sheep grazing as usual. Because Wusong was incorporated into the special municipality, the farmers of Tui 34, Tui 35, Teng 40, Teng 41, and other villages bordering Bao Shan County all coveted the cheap price of sheep, which was profitable, and because the municipal government had no clear ban on sheep, eight or nine out of ten people invested in purchasing sheep from places like Yang Hang in Bao Shan for raising. They disregarded public morality and arbitrarily formed groups to graze in the fields, causing great damage to crops. Liu Ziwen, a member of the Wusong Municipal Government Committee, after receiving reports from the local bailiffs and farmers of the various villages for the past two days, immediately sent personnel to investigate the sheep raised by farming families in the countryside. There were as many as five or six thousand sheep. At this early spring time, the crops are just budding, and if they are allowed to trample and gnaw, it will not only hinder the spring harvest, but the autumn harvest will also be greatly affected. Moreover, this situation is not unique to the Wusong district. It is assumed that the situation is largely the same in other rural districts of the city, which is of great importance to the future of agriculture. Therefore, yesterday, the Social Bureau of the Municipal Government was presented with the situation and requested that the Municipal Government immediately issue a proclamation banning farmers from grazing sheep in the spring, following the precedent of the Bao Shan County government, so as not to hinder agriculture.

County Government Orders District Offices to Handle Burial 176

Recently, Leng, the magistrate of Shanghai County, ordered that, since exposed coffins and corpses were everywhere in the county, and that some had not been buried for many years, which was detrimental to hygiene, the district chiefs were instructed to bury all exposed coffins and corpses, regardless of whether they had owners or not, before Arbor Day. The funds required, set at 100 yuan per district, have been officially notified to the property office to be allocated under the charity item.

Conclusion of Trial for Husband's Murder by Mercury-Laced Rice 179

Landlady Inevitably Suspected of Abetting

Last year, a foreign resident, Hou Yanji, was poisoned by his concubine, Hou Li, who mixed mercury into his rice in an attempt to murder him. Hou noticed something was wrong and shouted for help. The police sent Hou to the hospital for treatment. Because he did not ingest much, he was able to recover. Hou Li and the involved landlady, Li Wei, were detained and sent to the District Court for interrogation. It is now learned that the Procuratorate has completed its investigation and determined that Hou Li and Li Wei, who abetted her, were guilty of murder under Article 284, Section 1 and Section 2 of the Criminal Code, and have filed a public prosecution. Yesterday morning, Judge Qian opened a court to hear the case. Hou Yanji testified that on the afternoon of January 19th, at 3 p.m., his wife, Hou Li, called him home for dinner. Because he was ill and had a poor appetite, he complained that there was a lack of soup, and it was difficult to swallow the dry rice. At that time, the landlady, Li Wei, said that it would be better to use vegetable soup to mix the rice, which would be easier to swallow than dry rice. However, when he was about to finish eating, mercury appeared at the bottom of the bowl, and he realized that there was poison in the rice, which was why the taste was different from usual. He shouted for help in terror, and the police sent him to the hospital for treatment and saved his life. He asked for an investigation, and so on. After obtaining the testimony, the judge ordered the imprisoned Hou Li and Li Wei to be brought to the case. First, Hou Li testified that she had been having an affair with Hou Yanji for seven years. This time, she tried to murder her husband with mercury at the instigation of the landlady, Li Wei, who repeatedly urged her to buy mercury. She was confused for a moment and bought three packets of mercury and took them home. At about 3 p.m. that afternoon, her husband, Hou Yanji, was drinking tea in a teahouse. Li Wei urged her to call her husband back for dinner. She mixed two packets of mercury into the rice, and Li Wei helped her mix the other packet into the rice. Fortunately, it was noticed immediately and he was sent to the hospital, so he did not die. This fact was instigated by Li Wei, and so on. The judge asked, "Did Li Wei benefit from ordering you to murder your husband?" She replied, "Li Wei told me that after Hou was murdered, she would let me eat at her house and think of another way," and so on. Li Wei vehemently denied this. The judge asked, "Do you have any grudges against Li?" She replied, "No." The judge said, "Since there are no grudges, there is no reason for her to implicate you." Li Wei testified that this matter was entirely initiated by Hou Li alone, who wanted to murder her husband. She repeatedly discussed it with me in secret. I said that human life is at stake, so how could I do such a thing? Where is your conscience? However, she was determined to murder her husband, and I could not stop her. The judge asked, "Why didn't you provide this kind of testimony earlier? It is obvious that you participated in the murder plan. Even if Hou Li is implicating you out of resentment, then why did she admit that she went to buy the mercury alone and did not say that you went with her? She also said that she put two packets into the rice, saying that you only put in one packet. Judging from this, Hou Li's testimony is correct." At this point, the judge ordered prosecutor Zhu to come to the court to present the prosecution's intentions and requested that the designated lawyer Zhou Yu defend the two defendants. The judge then declared that the arguments in this case were over and awaited sentencing. The two defendants, Hou Li and Li Wei, were returned to custody, and Hou Yanji was dismissed.

Zheng Jinshan, a native of Funing, who lives at No. 7 Yishen Lane, Yaojia Stone Bridge, Zhabei, yesterday brought Zhang Wang, with whom he lives, to the 4th District General Office to complain, saying that he used to farm in his hometown. However, his wife was led astray by Wang, who lived with them, and suddenly liked to wear heavy makeup and fancy clothes. She secretly cut off her Lizhi hair and often went to amusement parks or movie theaters. The feelings between the couple, which were once strong, are now often strained, like strangers. A few days ago, she was led out for fun by Wang three times in a row and given a fur coat. However, on the 14th of this month, she disappeared. He has no relatives in Shanghai. Judging from the situation, she must have been abducted by Wang. Therefore, he brought her to the office to ask for an investigation. She often invited me to go out, and I could not refuse, so I accompanied her out twice. A few days ago, the plaintiff and his wife had an argument and said that he wanted to sell her. She was very angry and sobbed for a long time. (At that time, she said to me, "I (referring to the plaintiff's wife) don't want to live in this world anymore." I comforted her, but I didn't expect her to disappear the next day. So the disappearance of his wife is not my fault. As for saying that I gave her a fur coat, you don't know that I can barely feed myself, so where would I get the money to make clothes for her? All the accusations are unfounded. Please investigate." Director Jin thought that the statements of both parties were conflicting, but the case involved criminal prosecution, so he ordered them to be sent to the bureau for interrogation.

Small Cargo Ships Gather to Protest Inspection and Are Expelled 182

All types of boats in the city, except for punts and rowboats, which are simply constructed, have complex demographics among the boatmen, and have no legitimate business, have long been criticized by passengers on the Huangpu River. Therefore, the Municipal Government has decided to ban these boats that hinder traffic and has stipulated that no donations or taxes will be levied to limit their number, in order to seek a fundamental solution. In addition, boats with legitimate businesses should pay donations separately according to the prescribed grades, which goes without saying. However, small cargo ships carrying rice have completely different areas, tonnage, construction, and business nature from so-called punts. Now, someone is stirring up trouble, trying to cite the precedent of rowboats and demanding exemption from donations. They gathered at the Dongjiadu Wharf to protest the inspection and forced the same type of boats that had already registered and paid donations (about sixty ships) to join the commotion. The Water Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau believed that the actions of small cargo ships, etc., were detrimental to traffic. Merchants' Association Requests Permission for Street Vendor Association to Organize 192

The Merchants' Association submitted a report to the Central Party Headquarters yesterday regarding the organization of a trade association for street vendors. (Above omitted) The case originated from a letter from the Vegetable Stall Industry Branch on the 12th of this month, stating: "We have read in the newspaper that the Central Executive Committee has issued instructions to party headquarters in various provinces and cities, as well as a news item stating that the new Chamber of Commerce Law and the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law have been officially promulgated by the government. From now on, the organization of merchant groups should be carried out in accordance with the newly promulgated laws and regulations. Members of the original merchant associations, except for street vendors who are mobile and do not need to organize a group, are naturally included in the Chamber of Commerce and the Trade Association. We do not know if this is true. Our branch was originally composed of street vendors and is naturally included in the street vendor category. However, we have found that most street vendors in various places do not have a fixed base. Their mobile nature is self-evident. However, the situation of street vendors in Shanghai Special Municipality is different. Street vendors must report to the Public Security Bureau to designate a location, assign a number, and pay a license fee to the Finance Bureau. They are not allowed to move without permission. The same is true in the concessions, where the police handle it in the same way. Therefore, their nature is different from that of other street vendors and those in other places. They are not mobile. May we request your observation and submission to the Central Government, approving that the Vegetable Stall Industry in Shanghai Special Municipality, like small and medium-sized merchants, should still be allowed to establish an association for the purpose of judgment, etc." Upon investigation, the letter states that street vendors in this city must report to the bureau to designate a location, assign a number, and pay a license fee, and that after the number is assigned, they cannot move without permission. It can be verified that there are official records in the government offices. In its recent report to the Executive Yuan, the municipal government also stated this point and did not make it up. The claim that their nature is not mobile and that the situation is different from that in other places is reasonable. Street vendors belong to the category of small merchants. The general rules for merchants have clear provisions, but restricting their right to unite and defend themselves seems to be contrary to the principle of equality for all in national politics. According to the previous letter, the branch association resolved at the 37th standing committee meeting to submit it to the Central Government for review and approval. We hereby submit this document to your department for review and approval and request that you issue instructions for compliance. (Below omitted)

Gangsters Arrested at Chunjiang Hotel 195

Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the Municipal Public Security Bureau sent detectives to the special agency of the French Police Station, stating that, according to confidential reports from informants, several gangsters were hiding in the Yuebin Hotel at No. 1621 Avenue du Capitaine Thébault and the Chunjiang Hotel at No. 309 Caishi Street. They requested the dispatch of detectives to cooperate in the arrest. After receiving the report, the police chief immediately ordered several detectives to go together. They arrested Zhang Youmo (38 years old, local, driver), Zhang Shirong (30 years old, local), and three women in Rooms 25 and 35 of the Chunjiang Hotel and took them to the police station for verification.

Underground Opium Trade Operation Broken Up in Baoyu Lane 196

Fine of 3,960 Yuan

Shen Defu, Chief Detective Inspector of the French Police Station, Detective Inspector Chen Sanlin, Detectives Lu Jinchen and Mao Jinsheng, and Police Officers Lu Jinbao and Jiang Changwen, discovered that someone was running an underground opium trade operation at No. 35 Baoyu Lane, Caishi Street. They went there and seized two boxes of opium, weighing 198 pounds, worth 7,920 yuan. They immediately took Wang Ashui, who was trading opium, to the police station. The police chief ordered Wang to be released on bail pending further investigation. Yesterday, he was summoned to the French Court for prosecution. The police chief first reported the previous request to the court. When questioned, the defendant Wang Ashui confessed to illegally trading opium. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Wang to a fine of 3,960 yuan, which was confiscated. The opium was confiscated as well.

Hebei Fellow Villagers Association Held General Assembly Yesterday 203

The Hebei Fellow Villagers Association held the 19th annual general membership meeting in the front yard of the association's office at No. 1410 Ma Lang Road, Avenue Edward VII, at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than 300 people attended. Chairman Zhao Nangong rang the bell to open the meeting and conducted the ceremonies as usual. First, Chairman Zhao Nangong reported the purpose of the meeting and the various charitable activities held last year. Next, Secretary Chief Wu Shouyuan reported the detailed income and expenditure accounts for last year. Then, the executive and supervisory committee members for this year were elected. First, the presidium drew ten people from the sixteen designated people by lottery: Jie Fuchen, Li Weizhou, Wan Xuanzhi, Shen Xiaoting, Sun Naiqing, Ping Laozhai, Ren Heshan, Ge Qingshan, Dai Jianqing, and Wang Shouxian as executive committee members (nine incumbents, totaling nineteen including the above). Liu Fengshan, Zhang Chunong, Zhang Mingtao, Li Zhuxi, Qi Tiehen, and Zhang Xichen were elected as supervisory committee members. The decision was unanimously passed on the spot. Next, Shen Yingzhi temporarily proposed (1) that the association vigorously promote the establishment of Hebei fellow villagers associations everywhere, and (2) that the Hebei fellow villagers associations in various places should take Shanghai as the central organization in terms of united rule. Both proposals were unanimously passed by the entire audience. After the photo session, there were national martial arts performances and Peking opera singing to add to the fun.

The debtor's real estate listed below has been sealed and appraised. As the deadline has passed and no one has offered to buy it, in accordance with the previous price, it is reduced by 5% as the minimum price. It is now set to hold a bid at this court's fourth ballot box on February 28th. The bidding will be opened on March 6th. Any residents who wish to buy this real estate should submit a sealed letter stating their name, age, place of origin, address, occupation, and the price they are willing to offer. The highest bidder among the bidders will be the winning bidder. The winning bidder shall pay one-fifth of the bid price as a deposit on the same day, and the remaining amount shall be paid in full upon delivery of the property. Commercial News 208

The thriving business of Guanshengyuan's Photography Department: The main store of Guanshengyuan Food Company on Nanjing Road announced that the Guanzhen Photography Department, located on the second floor of the store, has always been known for its excellent photography of small art photos at four dimes each and four-inch registration-style art photos at one yuan and four dimes each. People from all walks of life believe that the photos taken are lifelike and are quite praised. Therefore, in terms of business, it has been catching up with its peers in the Nanjing Road area. Recently, the department expanded its internal scope and hired a strong photographer with rich photography experience at a high price to be in charge of art photography. In order to reward all sectors of society, special preferential prices are offered, with a 60% discount from February 1st to the 20th to provide preferential photography to customers during the New Year. Now that the deadline for preferential treatment is not far away, many people from all walks of life go to take pictures, and there is a great atmosphere of crowdedness.

The monthly awards of Mingxing Developing and Printing Society are announced: Mingxing Developing and Printing Society announced that the company held its first monthly prize drawing on February 15th, and the results were numbers 541 and 586, which are the winning numbers. The company is soliciting the above numbers. The winners are requested to send the numbered envelope along with a negative for enlargement to the Mingri Music Bookstore at No. 463 North Sichuan Road as soon as possible. The company will enlarge it as a gift, etc.

Taihe Malt Essence Cod Liver Oil sells well: The Yong'an Company on Nanjing Road announced that the pharmacy department of the company is doing quite well, especially Taihe Malt Essence Cod Liver Oil, which has the highest sales volume. People say that malt essence cod liver oil is the most famous brand, with great efficacy and excellent tonic power.

Theater News 209

The New Year's Eve Reunion Variety Show is scheduled to be held. Yigong Publishing House announced that the company was founded by the giants of the Chinese film industry. This year's New Year, in order to unite friendship, it is scheduled to hold a New Year's Eve Reunion Variety Show at the Central Auditorium on North Sichuan Road on February 23rd (Sunday) at 7:00 PM. Each ticket sells for one yuan. It is reported that the proceeds from the tickets will be used to establish a library dedicated to books on the arts for the reference of all sectors of society. The scheduled performances include Ms. Liang Saizhen's Cantonese opera, Ms. Wu Suxin's Catching Cao Cao, strongman Zha Ruilong's Thousand Jin Stone Lift, Ms. Xu Suzhen's large set of magic tricks, Mr. Zhou Kongkong's fan duet, and Xiao Mingxing Ren Chaojun's Iron Rooster, performed by actors Tang Xueqian, Xu Zhongxia, Lu Zhongxia, Ren Chiyu, Jin Xingyan, Mao Jinhan, Xu Zhongqiang, etc. from the Xifan Company, and Fang Peilin, Sun Shangxian, Wu Wanxiang, Ding Degui, etc. from the Xiren Company. The martial arts of the two companies have already had a good reputation on the screen. This time, the stage performance of Peking opera is completely real. The dozens of martial arts scenes are all thrilling. In addition, there are also a large number of male and female stars in the country to Shanghai. There are more than 20 programs in total, which will definitely cause a sensation in Shanghai. Tickets are sold on the third floor of Zhanji, diagonally opposite the Aode'an Theater on North Sichuan Road.

Da Guangming premieres New Love Style: Da Guangming Theater announced that in addition to the premiere of a singing and dancing giant film with sound, the theater, in view of the dullness of life, is eager to offer the audience a humorous and funny work. Therefore, it has recently brought in a famous film, "Funny Love," starring Ian Hunter, the protagonist of the previous "Conflict between the Sexes," and Charlies Kent, who is famous for his comedies. The wonder of their performance is self-evident, and the addition of the beautiful female star Catherine Crawford makes it even more exciting. The structure of the whole film is rigorous and the plot is tortuous. It is truly a rare work among sound films, and its in-depth portrayal of love and life issues is especially worthy of discussion and research by modern men and women.

Guanghua Theater premieres The Black Eagle Pirate: Guanghua Theater announced that the posthumous masterpiece of the late romantic superstar Fan Lun Tieniu, The Black Eagle Pirate, premiered at this theater on Mengnala Road last Sunday. It has been two days. Admirers of films competed to be the first. Therefore, before 2:00 PM, the front of Guanghua was already crowded. It can be seen that the film is precious. The film is only shown today and tomorrow. On Thursday, the meaty and fragrant Chen film "Sexual Heat" starring Clara Bo will be replaced.

The New New Opera House Election Committee: The New New Opera House in Ping Le Li, Er Malu, announced that the opera house has achieved excellent results since its establishment, and the club affairs are booming. The club held an election meeting last Thursday and publicly elected Chen Yunchuan as the president, Zhang Xinying, Cai Guirong, Tan Chuqing, Lu Desheng, Lou Shu, and Li Shiquan as the directors, Gao Zihao and Gao Ziying as the clerks, Pan Fengbo and Tai Mengying as the theatrical affairs officers, Chen Yucai, Li Caibao, Ren Hao, Tong Gu, and Hong Kui as the supervisors, Xue Hai Chou, etc. as the social officers, Liu Xiao and Fang Yunbiao as the teachers, Huang Weizhong and Pan Renzong as the instrumentalists, and Li Xiaomao as the drummer.

News from the Publishing World 210

Mr. Wu Guangda, a leading figure in the publishing and translation world of Ningbo, has had his translated work of the European classic "San Ning" published and is now distributed by Huatong Bookstore on Fourth Horse Road. The original book has translations in various countries and has sold extremely well in Europe, even going through dozens of reprints. It is said that since the publication of this book by Huatong Bookstore, the threshold has been worn through with customers, and there is a general feeling that supply cannot meet demand.

The Puyi Real Estate Company announced that the February issue of their real estate monthly publication is complete in content, beautifully illustrated, and includes several valuable maxims. Those interested in real estate conditions are invited to request it from the company at No. 50 Nanjing Road, and it will be sent as a gift.

Publication of Good Japanese Books: Everyone knows that Japanese is an important subject. However, modern Japanese has many cumbersome systems, and although there are specialized books, they are not unified. Scholars often focus on one aspect and lose sight of others, failing to achieve results. Now, Mr. Jiang Hui, a professor at the East Asian Tongwen Academy, has authored a new book called "Modern Japanese," which has a novel editing method and complete systems, allowing for self-study without a teacher. It can be used as a textbook in schools and is truly a good book. It is now being sold by Shan Bookstore at the end of North Sichuan Road.

News from the World of Painting and Calligraphy 211

The painter Lü Gongwang has returned to Shanghai from Huzhou. Mr. Lü Wang of Beiping has calligraphy that is vigorous and powerful, and has long been highly praised. He originally planned to increase his fees in the Gengwu year to benefit the poor, but in the new year, he was invited by a friend in Huzhou to write inscriptions for plaques. He only returned yesterday. He had already accumulated many written pieces last year, and this has further increased the backlog. It is difficult to increase the fees now, so he will temporarily maintain the original example from the Yi Si year and revise them in the summer. Those who admire him should take note of this. The general receiving address remains at No. 129, intersection of Ximen Road and Bai'er Road.

Collection of Childlike Hearts 212

I remember that last summer, the elementary school of the Patriotic Girls' School published a collection called "Childlike Hearts," which was very well received by readers. They originally planned to publish second, third, and more collections, but the training instructor, Guo Licen, accepted an invitation from Suzhou Girls' Middle School and Elementary School, and thus Mr. Guo left the Patriotic Girls' School to work at the Suzhou school. After graduation, most of the young writers dispersed, with about two-thirds remaining to continue their studies in the middle school of the Patriotic Girls' School. Although they were scattered like swallows and petrels, their spirit of unity remained the same, and they continued to work tirelessly in the arts. The enthusiasm for the first collection was already surging and boiling in their minds. Even outside readers often sent letters to inquire, showing that those who had read it were extremely concerned. The motivation for the second collection was their fuse. It is said that they already have a complete plan and are currently preparing various manuscripts, with Mr. Guo Licen still responsible for editing, and the second collection will be published in the near future. (Licen)

Guidelines for Art World Submissions 213

(1) Text should be limited to news, reviews, and introductions of recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature, both domestic and foreign.

(2) Pictures should be limited to recent works by new artists, both domestic and foreign, and related illustrations to the text.

(3) Photographs should be limited to works by domestic and foreign artists and various photographs related to the text.

(4) The number of words in each text should not exceed 3,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally, and the writing should not be sloppy. Western text should be abbreviated where possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw illustrations in the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate "Art World Department Receiving" on the submitted manuscript.

(9) Whether the manuscript is published or not, it will not be returned. If a return is required, it should be stated in advance, and sufficient postage should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for texts is divided into three types: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand words. The same applies to pictures and photographs per piece. Special manuscripts will be compensated separately.
